des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the division of the cure of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the parts where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things made by wounds are made by the point of the pierce, and the size of the tooth and the cuticle, or the lance, or the staff, or the spear, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or what is made according to the wounds of the body, like a plague that is made on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with the simplest wounds, as the remembering comes in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes or is born, and it is not broken, if it is caused by cutting or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubtlessly have an abscess forming:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if the head is becoming safer of the wound itself if it comes out little blood from the wound, and it is healthier on the opposite side of the affected part:
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And the patient avoids excessive consumption of wine and large pieces of meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not see better, if his meat is weak, and he does not drink wine, and does not eat cheese.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and puts the wound in oil, and if it comes out easily, it is washed with linen or rancid olive oil only, or with wine tincture.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if he does not wash the wound with oil, and puts it on the wound, it is fresh at all its base, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say here afterwards.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he moves the wound, and puts it on any bandages, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a spearhead and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be assembled by tents, if they can be assembled by stitching, if I say as belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is discovered on the bone, and it can be held only with one hand, then it is a fracture.

et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if blood has gathered in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without surgery, and it cannot be stopped with medicine, then the blood vessel should be cut. et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And do you put this powder on the wound that seems to have been burned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And how the powder should be applied is.
pren encens une partie;	Take some tinder and a part of it.
sanc de dragon II parties;	two parts of dragon's blood.
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	three parts of chalcedony, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and extract as much as it adheres well and joins with all its sand.

de la plaie dou col	of a minor wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes or goes and it is simple, but if there is no difference between the two and the collarbone or the artery is not affected.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the case, if there is no other means than to let nature take its course and make no restrictions, because it harms the nerves and pulls them back.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of such is with the brain, which is the more sensitive members.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but if the medicine is salted, like chalz washed in gentle water, and mixed with rose oil, and the wound washed again in gentle water, and other nails done this way, and moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, and the edges are not torn, then the cure as soon as it is healthy.

et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is closed, and the blood flows away, when it should not, and the limb is weak, and the cauterization is difficult;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the neck is closed, or the jaw, and the guide is kept, as long as the meat goes, if the bone is above the jawbone, and it is not touched but is returned according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then the strain is applied, and it leaves some scars, then the treatment of wounds is discarded as soon as it is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound makes an impression on the bone, if you wish.

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a lance or a spear wound, and the wound is deep, then look at the wound's depth and consult the surgeon about the patient's condition.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	And scars are known to be fatal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	If it is not properly shaped and fresh at all its joints, if it is not put on at the first hour with powder, and it is not held by the sore that does not worsen, and returns to the body, and the patient feels better.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	However, if I apply an attractive ointment and it is tied twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if there is no ointment, then put cotton in the wound for moisture and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm, and the patient does not have muscle twitching or shaking from the waist.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the proper arrangement, if you suspect that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Cure the wounds with tendons and other treatments as necessary to be healthy.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot be healed, and you suspect that it has formed an abscess, then...
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is done as it should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is of incision or contusion, and it is simple, or on the side, or at the back, if the treatment is done by the one who is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, of costure;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, of powder, and if it is embedded in the bone, and in pieces, if you want the wound to heal, and they are made to be if they are dissolved;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	If they do not heal, leave the wound exposed, and straighten the drawings.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And other wounds on other parts of the body are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	A sudden and severe pain in the stomach.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The dislocations of the stomach are large and numerous and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Of the large wound, no time does the intestine jump, or the intestines are torn, because of the insertion of others.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And the stitching is more painful, and never once is it better for the small wound than the large, because if one does not reinsert the intestines often, they are not reinserted in turns.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	For this reason, the intestines swell so much that they feel pain, if they return more frequently, and for this reason it is difficult to heal the wound, for it is hard to realign the intestines in their place like others have done.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you know that the rupture of the belly is in four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common ones come in the belly wound, and the other wounds of the chest and the rest are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more clean with the belly wound, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no inflammation in the intestines, and it is a simple matter to reset, this is done by one of the two following ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are twisted due to the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is swollen, you should cleanse it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a damp cloth only, or you can use hot water and add vinegar and salt, and rinse the intestines as much as they are swollen.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And no time has it been made to fasten this wining, and it is dead that it does not hold.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the blossom leaving, if the intestine is hot or cold and uneven, for this is the cause of the passage being narrow.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, then make a small wound in the plague with the instrument and take out the hemorrhages.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	The first treatment is dead that it is not big enough, for there is no need to cut it in such a great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the cause of the stripping.
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If a thorn penetrates the skin and is not removed, and it remains there for a long time, it may cause the following symptoms:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine springs out, if you put it back according to its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, because this is what is needed.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	If the wound is wide and located in the lower abdomen, it may be necessary for the patient to lie down on their back and raise their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	If the wound is located in the lower abdomen, it may be necessary for the patient to lie down on their back and raise their head and legs higher than their waist. The goal is to elevate the affected part above the other to reduce pain and swelling.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And it is necessary to manage these large and dirty wounds accordingly.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	The wound is small as you see, then take your hand and administer the pitious that stains all the rawness of your hand, and gather your lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	This is the common way to stitch, and you use a needle or more, according to the size of the wound's depth, then leave the end of the wound open and sew it with a thread as strong as it has;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two heads of the hide with the two heads of the sutures, which are loose from the hide, as long as you can pierce that part, and assemble the four ends of the sutures together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the thread of a double needle passes through the eye of the second part, then assemble the two heads of the wound, and then leave out two spaces, and then pass another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then continue to pull the thread of the needle as you have done with the first needle, and continue doing this according to what you are used to with needles, until all the wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And the needles should be sharp and not too large, because sharp needles close all the wound, and very large ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore, they must be sharp.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not necessary to thrust the nails too deeply into the flesh and hide, which do not close and cause the wound to protrude before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then close the heads of the nails, so they do not cause swelling in the patient at night, and put on or drape cloth at the nail heads to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching nails is more convenient in small wounds, because it does not cause an injury to the nail.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method is common, and it is that you sew together the two ends of the leather and the two ends of the thread with one nail or it has a strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	When you have perceived these four conditions assembled, reset the wire at the part where you began, in the manner we have described.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and insert a splice between each stitch of a large thread of a minor doe.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch saved the man, and I saw a wound that some had in their belly, which was caused by a cut, and it was a wound more than a palm of great size, and it had intestines several pales of great size, and it was the wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I opened the intestine and it had been there for 24 hours, and the wound was 15 years old, and I treated it and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And he saw that it would die, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not treat it with any remedy, as I am in the first stage where none is found and no medicine works.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put a piece of cloth soaked in wool over the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey as often as it is needed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I would tell you two ways of dressing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pull out the thread from the part that is most difficult to sew.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has reached the right side in the right direction, if you have pulled the needle or cut it or pulled out the thread, and then try to percerate another part of the part that is difficult to sew.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And if you understand this method, then follow the example of the barber who combs his beard, and leaves once with one part, and takes it back with another, until the hair is entirely combed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galen himself describes, is such that no one does it otherwise, by naturally bringing together the two parts, and applying one part of the hair comb to the other, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Choose a needle or haircomb that is appropriately sized, and carefully insert it into the flesh, and leave the two hair combs.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make sure it is firmly in place, and use the two hair combs.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then I will feel the other side of the swollen part, in two other points located on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most common way to sew and stitch.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this, and no one testifies to it, so we must sew the belly with two needles, or have thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And it must be sewn with one needle on one side and the other on the other side, in the same way as those who are sewing crooked.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And you should know that when the wound is in the belly, it is the stitching that is more painful than other belly stitches.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that when you touch the fresh wound with all its sand, if it has not moved, then it must be reset, and the intestine is turned, and it is good.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on the powdered earth char, and if it has not moved, then put on any poultice that is present, as long as the wound bows.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And tie the string, and be sure the shackle is tight, and the mirror.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as you would with others, as long as it is healthy.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	When you have no medicine, if you put it, as much as it comes out of the belly, it gushes out like water, and it is moved twice a day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no other craft than this one to treat wounds, which are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound is not a principal limb, then it comes to milk the lighter in oil of calamus or rose oil, and put it on the edges, and dry them;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or abscess in the wounds, and often comes, then the dressings should be changed with wine from Germany, and at the same time the abscess comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the percussion of the belly, and the scissors that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the veins that surround it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gum jumps from the wound, if it is reset as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is swollen and turns black, then you must reset the dark one that has veins and arteries, because it has bones and blood.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then pull what is between the ligaments and put the two heads down until it is loose to align the extraction as the gum jumps, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, if it can be restored by a few men, because I have seen that some were healed from the belly or abdomen of a lance.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And the wound was on the left side of the stomach, and it became ulcerated and formed a fistula, and in it was the egestion and the vomiting.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop refining until it was healthy, and I saw the results.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw the improvement, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there is no harm, but it delays in better conditions, and eats and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and no one knows that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be stitched in a certain way.
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	First, pull the wound apart, then stitch the corners of the wound, and when the wound has been stretched out, put the lips on either side of the wound to hold it closed.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then, the wound is closed, and it stays in place if it does not slip, then close the other end in the same way as before, until the wound is completely surrounded.
et cout la plaie.	And the wound is counted.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the intestines are infected in the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a very fine thread that is woven from the intestine of a beast, in the same way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this intestinal thread that is full of excrement, and then tie it to the end of this linen thread, then pass the thread through the needle, and count the intestine, and reset it in the dislocation;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this way of stitching is not feared that according to the way of marriage and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, then it is subtle and not healthy, so it should be treated with care.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula," and also if they are thin and have a narrow opening.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And the fistula is according to the nodulation that must be hard and painful, where one feels pain, and it is as fine as the tail of a feather.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never in a clear jump, and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and never small, and sometimes quite.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that all wound that is not healed, and there is no pain, it is only due to one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This is to know, by the slight pain of the wound or corse;
ou por sa malice;	or for malicious intent;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because he has hardened his teeth and bites them, which he does not let go;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or he has too much bite;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the thread is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is delayed in digestion, and delayed in health, and escapes by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	If there are wounds or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have shown all these causes, and signs, and remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The following lines are the translation of the given Old French text into English:
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Wounds that fistula come in all members of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For it has fistulas that come from large wounds, arteries, nerves, or the face, intestines, rectum, bladder, or any of the ribs, spine, or joints of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if it comes to the part of the member that belongs to the proper owner, and they are similar to this.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this kind are of unhealthy salvation, and only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there are no fistulas that do not come out of the body as I have said, and you are a doctor of the cure, and you see it, then take a tent of linen or iron, if you want; and if the fistula is straight, then do so.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is curved, then search for a fine tent of linen, because the threads will twist inside the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula is forced and you do not find it well by tents, then search for it with the other pertus, because the moisture is short of one pertus and makes it clean.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then, when you feel pain, know whether it is bone or flesh, and gently ask the patient to indicate where they feel the pain when you press with your hand, and the limb where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the limb where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or any of the limbs I have mentioned, if the coupe follows what I have said, and oste be the fault and the corrupted parts that are denoted;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then, when it is healthy, and the fistula is well sutured in the right place, if you cut in the same way, as far as you can, then you put fine tentacles in the medicine ague, and you thrust them into the bottom of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is excessively produced at the fons.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then he puts antiseptic agents in clean hands as much as possible.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not clean, then he cauterizes as we have said, and if the wound is corrupted by the fistula, then the copper.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not cause pain or limbs, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the wound is discovered and it has corrosion and blackness, as long as the corruption is all extensive, then the treatment of clean hands as we have said.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not clean, and the wound is deep, as we have said, ask what you are not able to do.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If dislocation occurs and you are able to do it, and remove all corruption, then restore the joint.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is in good health, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, then you should know that the corruption is too deep, and it will not improve.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other engine but a lashing of nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if it has small corruption and you remove it with thorn, if it is strained to the instrument that is suitable for this, and if it has more, if you remove them all, do not leave any.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if the moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear, then cope and moisture and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	If you do not clean the wound at once, then put on something to absorb moisture and leave it on until the pus comes out of the bones, and then if they become lighter, the bones will be easier.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	If it is large bones, such as those of the thigh or knee, if you only clean it so long as the blackening is all over, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	If it has a large part of corrupting, and comes to the bone's end.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it is necessary to sew and cover all the corruption, and then treat it as much as possible.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of an example of a fistula that came to the leg of one man, if you pay attention and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man who, at the age of XXX, had a pain in his leg for a reason that came from the chest, so much that the materials came to the leg, and he was fled by a large abscess, and there was no cause to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but they overwhelmed them so much that the abscess overflowed, and it corrupted the materials, and became a fistula, and there came out of it blood and pus from the belly and moisture from the chest;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And for the next two years, and no one had any skill in the art of hands, as long as I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines used to cure it, and what rotted due to the pustules of great heart;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red in his youthful chest, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of these holes, and then checked all the holes, and found that some went into another part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I thought, and in one of the pustules I found a part of the bone, and I discovered it was rotten and hollow, and it came from the hollow of the bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was he who appeared from the rotten bone, and I made sure there was no other corruption, for that was what I stayed for;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound of the soda patient with long ties, and could not be closed.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I reopened it, and found the bone as before, and discovered that the infection continued in the bone, and dressed it, and then closed the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not cut all the way through the bone, and it turned to one side, then I restored it with drugs.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healthy and closed quickly, and I no longer wished to open the wound because of the patient's weakness, which could not endure it, and for fear of death that I had caused him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For since the blood was often evacuated, but it was completely cured, and there was a hard char on the bone, and it was well positioned and had no harm or contradiction in any way, neither in the air nor coming out.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken at any joint of the arm, then it should be set in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Tie the cloth, and pull on the end of the bone that is open, and command it not to extend further up.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	Then tie another large loop on the second loop, and tie it around the bone that is sticking out, and make sure the end is in the correct position. Then draw the broken piece of the bone back into the socket, and cut off the excess, so that it does not break the bone.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	Then put a sponge or a piece of cloth on the bone to cover the broken piece of the bone.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to soak as much as possible and can be seen and felt the corruption, and soak again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the environment or in a part of it, if the chest is completely opened.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the bone in place, and then be of one part of another the corruption, and let the soaked part of the corruption be as long as the bone we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, if the corrupted joint is closed, and it is the bone or it contains another part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is found in the continuation of the second joints, if there is no other cause but darkness.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if corruption is found in the finger or toe, if it is not strong, but it is necessary that you investigate that corrosion, to see how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And cleanse it in all ways that you can, but the vein or nerve will not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And sharpen the scalpel and the threads according to the appearance of the bones, and their size, thickness, and width, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	For this reason, it appears to adjust to each appearance of its tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And you should be confident that the operation will show the instrument you will use, according to the knowledge of this art, and it testifies to the methods of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you lack the instrument you should have according to what is needed.
dou feu	The first sentence to translate is "Ou
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder will become loosened either due to weakness or due to decay.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated the corrosion by medicine, and it does not improve until the member reaches the shoulder or the corrosion comes, if the malady is caused by death or by malice, which is greater, by the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	When the signs appear that the limb becomes black, if it seems to be from burning heat, and it turns red after turning black, then corrosion spreads throughout the member, and it takes hold of all parts.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you feel burning pain, and it is due to the impact of some beasts' venom, like that of a sea scorpion and weasel, and the corrosion reaches the tip of the finger, then the cure is not to give in to the pain and come to help with your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to your hand, if the cure is given to the joint, then the corrosion does not come to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	If it comes to the arm, if the wound is at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	If it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no way to save it but the quantity of its courage.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And so it is when the corrosion comes or pain.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes in the first joint, if the wound is after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	If it comes with pain, if the wound is all pain.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	If it goes up the leg, if the wound is at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	If it comes from the thigh, if there is no other way but to kill the patient with pain.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	The patient should gently bend the limb if it is not already bent, and then hold one end of the limb steady while another person holds the other end. This should be done until the bone is discovered between the two bones.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then wrap the limb with cloth, and if it does not touch the healthy skin, then go to the physician for another injury and infection.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the skin immediately, or if you put on any restraining powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as soon as it is completed, then tie the affected member with a flexible cord, and treat it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to my home in short:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	it happened to my home a darkness that seemed to be on fire, and this corrosion came first in the morning, consuming all the property.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corrosion, if it could be stopped from spreading, and it was saved.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and later, when it returned with the hand, and it came to me, and I did certain things after the disinfection of the corrosion, but it could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and I say that I will hold his hand, and I do not hope to feel the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die because the strength of his arm was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate and returned to his land, and took hold of his hand and was cured.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have never heard of anything better than this, because it is the best way.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never has an abscess come in the charnut, and it takes as long as it takes to gather many arrows.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they pierce and break, and by jumping the arrows, and make them give way to the wound, just as some slaves.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	The patient's clothing that is cut is also as delicate as silk, and does not cut through the bone or nerve, and such disease is called "hernia", and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	However, if it is so long that it reaches the bone in front, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	If the clothing that has been cut is entirely removed, and at the same time it is as delicate as silk, like some drapes.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and should not be cut for fear of corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are engaged and the clothing is cut, and corruption is not at the front, and the hair is very thick, then the treatment of cleansing is necessary.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	1. Pay attention to the size of the breasts, and the belly that is in it, since it is of a strong odor, therefore the clitoris is treated with Egyptian medicine that has been made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	1. Take asafetida, oil, and turmeric, in equal parts, and cook them in a pot over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes thicker than honey:
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	1. Then use this according to your need, and make it into an ointment and honey, and apply it to the breast, and draw out the pustule:
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	1. Leave the medicine on for two hours, then draw it out by squeezing:
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	I will make this many times, until the breasts are deformed and the pain is unbearable.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And never has it been clitoralised with ash, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you ignite grapevine ash, and the ash is poured, then it flows, and in clitoralisation, as long as you feel that the breast is well deformed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear it, and the Egyptian medicine does not cause ash, then clitoralise with ash and honey or if there is a little litharge in the mixture.

que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	That the bowel moves lightly and leaves nothing of the bowel.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to strengthen the stomach, and they are hung on the loose linen that covers the entire stomach.

et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then remove the morning or evening, and when you notice the wound, if it changes to another fold, and change the ointment;
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become wet and indigestible after a long journey, it is advisable that the breasts are not milked.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the venoms are subtle and short after a long journey, do not despair about your health, as your health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For he has many horses that delay in making char for his wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if he bows indigestibly after one day, if it seems that the breasts have not settled yet;
