pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	If the injury is definite, and it is treated with rose oil, and the wine is equal in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	Then it is cooked and used.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And the same thing is made with honey that is cooked and increased when definite injuries are not present, or you take a knife and aloe and incense, and the broth, and the powder on the honey when it is near the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	Then they apply ointment and wrap it around the wound, and it is never administered by an astrologer for long, and roots of the celestial lily, which is also like fine flour and earth.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And they use either simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	They boil them, and then powder them, and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is large, and not cured by this treatment, then you should know that corruption has set in, and it makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard members, or in the joints.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the care of the fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that often occurs due to the infection of the thumb or big toe, or by chance in other parts.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	When it is inflamed, and it is not taken care of, if an abscess forms, and it runs and pours out blood until it reaches the root of the toe, and by chance it runs all the way;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion to the bone, as soon as it comes with pain, and the head of the joint is large, and the color is changed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, if you cover all the excess that is made from the finger, then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail is pressed against the bone, and it begins to prickle, and bleed, then you should remove the part of the nail that points at the bone, and cut it off high up, and carefully and lightly apply fire-and-corrosion medicated ointments all over;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the care of burns should be taken when it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, and it is removed, because as much as the bone corrupts and becomes, so it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If you see the second knuckle corrupt, if the copper is in I of us as it was said before, then the cure once it is healthy.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	If it is frozen, and stop, and it feels great pain, then it comes that you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the bone that is spatulate and hard in half, and make sure the cut does not reach the bone, for the patient will feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, then put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the dislocated shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocation that occurs in the hands of some men by chance is quite rare, and by chance it can be doubled, and never once it can be broken, and no one is born in the root of the jointure, or the birth is in any of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who do not have any other pain in the second knuckle and do not move, and those who have pain in the joint of the second knuckle by chance move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of the one who is tight so is light, in part manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	size it from its root a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who finds in the root of the joint is grievous to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold tight copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the case where the head of the shoulder is dislocated from behind, if you can first cover the joint with a clean cloth, then cover the bone with a suitable cloth, and then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The causes that come are either from birth, or from wounds, or from burns, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If they cover that the copper covers the soured, if it must be repaired according to their natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tent or draped softened in oil rose, that it does not sweat.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of cloth subtle, as it is sour, if it comes.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The patient comes to none of its two with the hand if it is not hot enough, as it should be.
des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Thick veins are heavily wrapped with excessive melancholic fullness, coming from more and more corpulent members.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often in the legs of those who go to church and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must never administer any purge of colic, and then the proper dose of the basilicon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One way is to hammer, and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to tie the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, the hot leg is raised with great force, until it is large and not subtle, then the other leg is tightly wrapped with the hair of the tail, from the part below the knee to the groin.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein at one point, either at the first, second, or third, of a large size, then take and draw out the dark blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as you can, as much as the patient's strength allows.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then tie it off, and order that it be painted with black meat juice.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And continue the evacuation and cleaning as the veins become clear, and inform the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The lesions of the affected area are treated in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Shave the patient's leg, if it has hair, then put it in warm water, and make the leg red and swollen by applying heat to the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If you do not have any bread, if the fire cautery is used, and then the cloth is placed in the vein at the long end of the thigh or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then apply the cloth to the gouge, and burn each part of the vein as it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see red and black, and when it enters or leaves, it seems as though it is a thick string;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then cut the cloth below the knot, as soon as it is loosened from the cloth, and then place it in another part of the thigh, and then pull it out in three;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scorch the leather on the vein as much as it appears, then smooth it with the rasp, just as you have done, and it can be used for another incision, just as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut a larger size, or more than you are used to, then smooth it, and carve at the sharp edge, then trim and smooth the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract the larger size, as much as it will fit, then smooth it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot extract it, and if it sticks to the skin so much that it requires a needle of great force double, then cut it and trim it, and remove it from the wound, and turn your hand over and over, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from being cut, for if it is cut, and it cannot be sewn or lifted, it harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated it all, put on the wound the fine hair of the plague with wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and keep it until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the wound is tight and twisted and assembled, and it is not straight, as we have said, then if you cut it roughly, but do not cut it straight,
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it will be like we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron that is cut when the vein is cut, and it does not cut too much, so as not to cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a large spider's web, because if it were small, it would cover the vein, but if it is large as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein of the arm.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is ensnared in limbs, in hot parts or no herbs or trees, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it naists another part than in limbs, and there comes a scurf that comes from the hide, as if the snake's belly comes out and turns, ensnared between hide and char;
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	When the signs of the beginning of this wound are visible if it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes color, and begins to bleed, and like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is opened, if you wrap it around a piece of plait from one and a half to two and a half inches long, and the noe, and leave the plait on the leg, and all times when it is not in its place, if you ensnare the plait and the noe;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, if a part of it is cut off, and it wraps around the remaining part, and does not cover its root as much as it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	If you cut it off, it will enter the chest, and bring forth pus and filth or blood, and serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For that reason, it is necessary that it be treated quickly and often, and nothing or a little remains of the head.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there is no time for this vein when it is treated with your hands of one to ten, or more, and some have come to me, from which it was ten, and if you cut it, if blood comes out, and the wound is not closed, then everything will be lost.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter that is densified be seen, and apply the medicines to the skin without any food for one day, then the cure is done as with the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never have hands rain on this vein, and at the same time when it opens in the joint or the other, and then comes out with pain, and which drops rain;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat the wound as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of verses that are born between leather and skin
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "beef disease," because it often happens to cattle, and is a sharp pain that runs between the skin and the bone, and goes up and down the entire body, and is felt all over the limbs as long as the hide remains on the bone or is removed, and jumps;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is caused by excessive humor of certain substances, such as worms, snakes, and leeches, or intestines.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And one wonders about its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it enters the brain, by chance it comes out, and destroys the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drawn out, if not possible when it will be.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it comes to pass that you lie the leg down and out of a tight wound well, then pull up and cut it, and turn it in front in the chariot, and you do not sew it, if the cauterization by fire is done, as long as it burns;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm he can do, if he cuts the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see him coming or approaching the oil, he will forcefully cut it off, then pull it out, and cut it off.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to use the physician's hands to dissolve the powders of liquid medicines for the human body, and to avoid eating fatty foods for nourishment.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from winding
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "wakiri" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to no part of the body, but spreads from one part to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I see what you have said.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a female patient, and I saw her arm, and I saw a small pimple in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And afterwards, I saw it growing faster than anything, as if it were live silver when cut from the bone.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain left that bone, and it twisted in the shoulder, and then a little later, it curved throughout the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it twisted in front of the body, just as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wished for this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Indeed, I wanted to make sure that she wanted to move the pain from one bone to another, but I could not do it, as I see in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	I thought it was because the woman had loose hair, and the veins were exposed, and for that this restraint appeared necessary.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	It did not occur to me that this reasoning was not applicable to those who have loose hair and veins returned.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	When you see the cure of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, should it open as we have said, if the joint does not move much, and then cut as far as that restraint is necessary at the shoulder;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the shoulder.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you do not see it with your eyes, if the cure of this which causes the restraint is like pills, and pills of sassafras, and similar things;
des saiettes	The term "des saiettes" translates
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The sails are various, depending on their appearances and the wounds of the body or they choke.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of its kind is that it has some with large points, and small ones, and hairs, and sores.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with double angles, and of those with long tongues, and of those where it has pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which does not fit in any member, but fits in two ways.
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or if it has hairs in the principal member, like the head, liver, spleen, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	If it does not fit in any of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears, you will know.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it happens that you resist the extraction of this arrow, because the death comes after in many attempts.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when you see that it does not seem to be hurting, and the arrow is not hurting in front, then cut it off, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a fractured skull when the arrow pierces the bone is that it breaks and the head falls away, and the part where the skull was is dark, and there is scotomy and soreness and swelling and pain in the limbs, and inflammation and pain in the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of the cole.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and by chance it lacks nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance the word and voice are lacking;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and a jump of the white moist wound resembling a frog's, and similarly like a horse's snort;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign appears, if you hold the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is pulled out or cut is that it is near the left cheek, and it feels as if it has been struck with a hard object, but not seen;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow is quiet like a frog's, and in dark red blood, and comes cold and very cold, and sinks:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The patient does not doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arm that is not moving is that there are no signs of inflammation from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the face turns pale, and he gasps for air and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead enters the shoulder blade, it may damage the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and suffocation.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and they move all the limbs of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the dislocated shoulder is the stomach, by chance if it jumps from the wound, nothing indigestible of the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the dislocated shoulder is the belly, and in a single jump through the small intestine, if there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead enters the bladder, and the urine is ejected in a sudden gush and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	The wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if the face, neck, shoulder, spine, shoulder blade, back, and muscles, and the limbs appearing similar, are only according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the flesh or artery, and it is not exiting, as I will tell you if I can, because you are making such a face.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	I have seen a man with an arrowhead that was shot into the shoulder bone.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it, and from another side, I removed some fat from the ear, and it was not very painful.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And then to a game a arrow that fell in the grease of the olive oil soaked the paper soaked, and the arrow was replaced, and it could not reach but only to the tip towards the enemy, and it was the arrow very large like a Turkish bow, at all I made it light weight for the ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And if the patient is healthy, and no accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And then to an arrow in the throat of a Crestian, and it was the Arabian arrow for the ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew the barbs, and very subtle when I passed it, and it was healthy for the Crestians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And there was a wound on his shoulder, which was swollen or bloated, and he thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then if it did not change its position within XXX days,
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I dressed the wound, and stitched it, and the patient left, and there was no further complication.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a man has a wound on his shoulder or back, and the wound is infected,
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and did not heal the wound, and did not maintain its natural position, and did not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if another man has a wound on his face, and the wound is infected,
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	It takes a long time to endure great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and there are other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And once a arrow was removed from the arm of a king's son, who had it stuck in his flesh and it was slanted to the left side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was fully removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for the treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to remove it with all my skill and did not feel any pain.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a sharp and painful sensation in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was the tip of the arrow that I touched with my tongue, because he did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the lesion of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I pressed the injured hand, and closed the wound on the right side, and it took a long time for the patient to feel the pain in his limb;
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied the medicine for the wound, which was overturned, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow that was embedded in the shoulder.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I closed the wound with the corrosive medicine, as the head of the arrow was visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it takes well for the end to last for four months, and then it is exhausted if the wound that I have closed with nails is not healed by both sides, and cannot be cured.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I did not stop refining and engineering ways of extraction, as soon as I took it with well-made nails, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, as I treat the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Therefore, I restored it, and it was sore from the wound, and the pain of the patient was relieved.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I said the quality of extracting some arrows, if you apply your care to what I shall tell you, for the books cannot make everything look perfect.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the skilled masters compere well with a few great things, and with what is present and lacking, true nine operations, and seven instruments, at the descent of things strained which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are made flat according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the hand or they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes through the eye or it enters, is an arrow that enters into the flesh, and it has never been dislodged once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, if it leaves it as is when the char is entirely burned and becomes unpleasant;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot be removed if left alone for any length of time, and each joint must be moved;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and therefore it jumps, and if it does not jump now, if it is pierced through at all points, as long as the char is sharpened, and then it will be drawn out;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the side, and it will come out through one of the bellies of the liver, or some other accidents that I have mentioned to the surgeon:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If it is not burned, but left as it is, as long as it is even after several days, for if the arrowhead comes out too soon, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the dislocation is not caused by the bone alone, and does not cause any other injuries, and the patient has had no previous accidents, then the surgeon should intervene.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it becomes very thick and cannot be extracted further, if the patient is in serious condition, as I have said.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is returned to the shoulder, and if one cannot see it, if they wish for all of it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, if there is no instrument that can be removed.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you do not feel it because of the wound, and the arrowhead is not removed, if the patient suffers greatly when the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	When you cut the tendon, and if it has ears in the tendon, then if the bone that is marked with II part of the muse where you cut it, and then break or crush the ears of the tendon as much as you can.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And carefully, even if you do not break the tendon, you should pull it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the bone is still wet until it is read, then pull it out, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the dislocation comes out of place, and it does not return to its original position, then you should not do what we have said in this chapter for the cure.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And you should be warned of the incision on the nerve and the vein, and put in an emergency situation where you can cut the tendon safely, either quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	The patient should be placed in the form it was before the injury occurred, as this is the greatest help to him. And if you do not want to do this, then he will be placed according to the sign that shows you what to do.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The injury comes from another side, or the patient has not opened anything of his own, or the skin is swollen in some place that can be seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	The wound should be opened as much as possible so that the thorns can take hold, and then it should be extracted.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If the pain is now intense.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If the bone is held in place, if the hand turns around as it enters the bone, until it expands the bone, then it should be pulled out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be removed, then leave it alone and then continue the extraction as soon as it hurts again.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	If the wound is from an arrow, it is cut open and cleaned; if it is not infected, it will heal. However, if there is doubt or fear, many die.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	If the wound is deep, and you see instruments being administered, if the tip of the arrow enters the handle of the instrument, it should be removed immediately.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If the wound is further deepened, and the tip of the arrow enters the handle of the instrument, it should be removed immediately to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is lodged, then you must remove the entire shaft or the venom if it is still inside. Then, treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	If the wound is in the chest, abdomen, or groin area, and it has healed, if it becomes inflamed, apply a poultice.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	Et keep the vein and the nerve, then extract it, then close the wound, and make sure it's done properly.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it as soon as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the arrowhead's points used to treat wounds is similar to the beak of an owl, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are several ways to do it.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the wound.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed hair is similar to that of an owl's beak, by inserting it at the tip of the arrowhead, as shown in this figure:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tines for insertion and removal is similar to this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Veins that are healthy are XXXI, but if there are XVI, it means:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two bands that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herb" chambers.
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And the two arteries that appear in the two temples.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two wounds that are in the two eyes of the two hairs, which are called "aspirations
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the wound that is in the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the wound that is at the top of the head.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two girdles which are off.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the wounds that are in the lips of the mouth, which are called "angleworms".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the wounds that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The wounds that are commonly known to be five in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the temporal wound, which is on the left side of the cheek, and it is called the "temporal wound" by the people.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the dislocation is called "fast" and is composed of the cranial and basilar parts, and they call it the "vein of the joint" in common language.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And if the basilar part is on the west side, and they call it the "vein of the abdomen" in common language, and it is located under the muscle, and it is the one that opens manifestly into the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvage vein is the one between the auricular and the anular vein, and if it rains.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg, there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is the vein that is opposite the coronary artery and the pouch of the left side of the chest, and the second one is the vein that is at the ankle of the right side of the chest.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "cesna", which is on the other side of the ankle.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three veins different from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears if helped by old catheters and removals.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the quality of the veins that is, as I say, and it is that you rotate the head of the patient and rub the leg or the veins are of a rough fabric.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then the patient's neck becomes red, as long as the two veins are visible behind the ears in the two legs depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	1. "If you feel the knot tightening, and if you feel pain in your shoulder, then loosen it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	2. "Then take the scalpel, and cut through the vein as close to the bone as possible, then gently hold the vein with your hand all along it, and compress and squeeze the area until you see enough blood, then stop the bleeding as much as you can.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	3. "Then hold the wound closed until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	4. "I have already said the incision and cauterization or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	5. "The health of the two arteries in the temples, if they are old and dry, and hard, and have become accustomed to the corse of the tears, then let them be removed.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and you judge its health if it is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient pulls on his chest, as long as the eyes open widely.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pain in your belly, and then signs of distress.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then gently press on the vein at the top of your belly, and remove the lancet, and gently press on the vein and the wound, as you have done in the other two veins, and make sure to draw out enough blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the belt, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then you form a poultice, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their treatment and extraction, or beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the forehead is as valuable as that of the head's cranium for ancient diseases of the face and migraines, and wounds.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is that the patient pulls his neck with force while the forehead is exposed.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "forceps," whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the forehead, and hold it firmly with your hand or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then the surgeon cuts the shoulder collarbone, and the vein is tied as soon as it is sound and never once with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it only requires the flame to be too hot.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the wound is safe because the bone is close, and by chance the flame breaks when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The safety of the two veins that are in the two arms is helpful for the wounds, and the tongue, and the gums, and the mouth, and diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their safety if the patient suffers from pain when pulling his shoulder by twisting any limb, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then comes the correct way, and it is the straight path, a small gap, a wide one, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it may be broken.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a clean cut, as much as you are able, and then sew it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The correct way of the vein is not always true, and can also be dangerous, and other diseases of the face, such as scarring and wounds that come with age, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the wound if it is the patient's skin that is strained, then press the neck with your left hand, and take the subtle flame, and close the eye in the space between the two eyes, because the vein does not open well, and now it will start to cut.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not alert too much, and make sure to draw out enough blood according to your need, then let it rest a night as it is most restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	and this salve is useful for the relief of headaches, and at the beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for eczema, and corrosions, and herpes, and boils:
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the salve is that if the patient pulls on his neck with both hands, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master being above the patient's shoulder, and the patient being on his side, then draw out the vein widely, then cut it with a sharp knife, as much as possible according to your skill:
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then, I did another part in the other vein, then removed the ligature, and stretched the veins slightly, so that the patient's pain would not increase.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips of the deer if they help to close in the mouth, and corruption of the genitals, and cracks of the lips, and sores and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And judge the health of the patient if it is necessary to tie the gauze in front of you, and stretch the neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the cheek, and look at the veins, one of which is on the left cheek and the other on the right, and you can distinguish them by their color and because they are thin and dark-colored.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	1. If you do not know how to do it, and you are in doubt, then try the largest one of each part, and make as many incisions as possible, because this is a different method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	2. If the tongue is injured after the head is treated, and it is at the throat, and there are diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth.

And if the patient is healthy, and the patient has fallen between your hands before the sun, and you touch the tongue, and look into each corner of a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	1. If done correctly on both sides, and not too forcefully, as the arteries are small.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	2. The veins that are usually cut are healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	3. either by pricking at every part of the flame, or by making a small cut, and are called "anethums";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	4. and are wide and thin according to the widening and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the burned face is such that it is not named, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	5. and has skill in opening flat veins with large clots of blood, and those that contain large clots and trouble.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	6. and it is the form of the small arterial cut:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle applied, and it is safer for the subtle veins, or if there is subtle citrin sang in them.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The health of the basilican vein, which is one of these veins, if it helps with diseases that are deosy the throat, and the collar, and the belly, and the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the patient to take advice and avoid the artery that is deosy.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he presses the artery, and the blood comes out, then it is necessary to stop the pain, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it should not be too many pricks of the flame, but trimmed as possible.

ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	If you do not want any rain from it, or if you are healthy in the vein of the arm, take the bone out.
elle apert manifestement;	It is open clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the forceps at the fire, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the bone of the limb, then it is necessary that you hold the arm and touch the bone as much as you can feel the pulsation.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the bone and then hold the arm and cut the vein with a hot forceps.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And be careful not to injure the artery when you see the bone enflame, because it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	The patient must let the hair grow long and even for the fire cautery.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	If you see coming out of the top like the urine of a child, and it is red and subtle, it is without arteries.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Do not dislocate the shoulder, and hold your hand far away, then observe if it does not move unsteadily, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	If you pull on the arm and let go, and do not move the patient's shoulder.

Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	If it does not become unstable, and you become weary, and the physician is not present, then if the artery is open, because the head of the shoulder will return.
et estainche li sans.	and it is painful for him.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a scalpel, and cut, and then take one of the halves and tie it well to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if it is painful for him, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, if the remedy helps to alleviate the pain, as we have said, with powders that relieve pain.

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The health of the vein in its environment is aided when it treats sanguineous pain and corporeal distress, because it is composed of basilica and cerebral, as we have said.

et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this cut nerve opens many times, and if it does not open by any means, then it is necessary to sew with the old instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And you should examine the nerve in your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is blood flowing between the two veins, if it is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the head helps, which draws blood to the head and helps the limbs.

Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	1. All ways, it is necessary to make the joint more flexible, and do not cause pain for the first time, and one resumes.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	2. And by chance, some people find that their joints become more flexible, but it does not cause pain the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your perception.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	3. The first thing you should know for health, if it is healthy, is not to spoil it by keeping it in good condition and avoiding diseases coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	4. And make the health in one of the three veins that are cut:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	5. That is to say, cephalic, fasten, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be healthier at the beginning of prayers, and in turn, and in yoga after mixing, when the sign of fullness appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And it should be healthier on the first day or the second, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The health that is maintained with diseases has no fixed duration, but when the patient is in bed or out of bed, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary for the children to be healthier than fourteen years old, and for women who carry no more than a quarter of a month after the ninth month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Necessity does not apply to those who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some appear healthier, in whatever way that may be, if it comes to causing the intestines of a light child to become distended, if there is a lot of feces retained, then the veins do not have unnecessary intestines that are harmful to the principal members.

Then the physician moistens the cleaner with a little oil, then places her left hand on the vein of the patient's arm, as far as she can reach, so that the vein does not bleed. The vein does not hurt.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that feel like cords to the physician, and if they are so tight, then they are easily compressed by pressure, so that when one places the cleaner at the vein, it retreats from the vein and cannot be opened, and then it is this one.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If the vein is pricked, and the wound is too tight, for it is necessary that the surgeon be informed in these matters.

s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant. Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the saved hand of the right hand is better than all diseases of the stomach, and it is this way.
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	1. To hold back the hand, and cut with a hot iron, as long as the vein is bare, if it can be reached.

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The patient's hand that holds the remedy is most suitable for treating mouse disease, and I do everything as I have said for the other hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy of the soap is suitable for all diseases that are unpleasant to the body, such as diseases of the lungs, retention of fluids, and disease of the legs, and old wounds, and similar diseases.

et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And if the vein is at the ankle, and due to pressure from the foot it starts to swell.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	If the swelling is small or large at the ankle, it is not good.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you have swelling at the foot, if there are nerves that are exposed, and it is painful to walk, as it is to cross a bridge.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the old veins be severed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot have children from your beloved spouse, and the wife is pregnant again, and the wound of the vein is well-healed; then leave the vein alone.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the swelling returns for the second time, if it is only a small amount, because the foot is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and I will make a poultice of the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The first line of the translated text is: "The pain in the sciatic nerve is at the ankle, and its cure is in the relief of the toothache, when it is due to blood evacuation.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And judge the quality of his health if he is in cold or bath, and draws out of the ankle IV when twisting, because otherwise it will not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it is opened, whether the patient is healthy in all ways that you can think of, and through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is worth copying if the patient understands it, as it is written, and it is returned to the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not copy, whether the patient is healthy in no way that has been opened or done, and to the small door, and it will give you some nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make as much evacuation of blood as you see, and then release the limb, and put on cotton and tighten.
ele est maintenant sanee.	The patient is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of childbirth pains
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suction devices are made of horn, or iron, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And suction is performed in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction, which is made by cutting, is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is totally burned, or by fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And this suction, which is made by cutting and extracting blood, is done in twelve hours of the day, with some being all the same, while others are different.
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the other is removed from the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more in the other shoulder;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suture of the corner;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suture of the two shoulder blades;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suture of the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the sutures of the elbows;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the sutures of the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the sutures of the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suture does not touch any vein, only thin wounds that are scattered throughout the chest, and therefore it is not able to cause harm, as we do with a wound;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is necessary that it be maintained, neither too much nor too little fire, in no disease that comes from excess, as long as the heart remains whole;
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity of diseases comes to visit, or by habit, if the midwife visits each hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and also in every ten;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have to visit, have heavy burdens;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if there are those who, when they come to visit, have fullness and inflammation in their face, in their cheeks, and in their neck, and pain in their limbs;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who come to visit with a fever in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If they have such wounds that prick, and see blood and pus and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and also when it is mid-month, we order them to rest after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the patient is aided by the girth of the belt... that comes as it does to the wounds, and it can only be after the evacuation of all the blood.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in the head of the patient's health, and it can only be when it is used for a cold complexion or if it has charcoal, because this does great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and that's why the physician only uses it when he has cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often become ill, then become obligated, and therefore it is necessary to shorten the rest period due to the fear of obedience.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The first line of the text translates to: "The ventilation of the chest is in the neck of the healthy cord and for this reason it is in the relief of the bronchial cough, and also for the fever and the sore throat, and for all the inflammations.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The second line translates to: "And it is recommended to bind it tightly, because if it is too tight, it can cause discomfort in the stomach or abdomen.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The third line translates to: "The ventilation of the collarbone is in the neck of the healthy spine and for this reason it is in the relief of the headache, and also for the toothache and strangulation, and for the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the neck of the healthy spine.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you command the surgeon to express his hand when putting it, so as not to cut the artery, and to avoid further damage to the wound.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windings of the gums do not reach the disease of the mouth, and the corruption of the genitals, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the lips of the dry lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cold and wetness of the shoulder joint causes inflammation and swelling, which can lead to serious health problems if not treated immediately. The affected area must be treated promptly to prevent further complications.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The windings of the cheeks are as much as three fingers of the arms, because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to cut too much in front, because the patient's face is naked and does not know how to cut nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction that is used at the groin if it causes pain and other diseases, and it is necessary that the suction be large and deep, with a stone-like texture, capable of properly drawing.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it is too fine, it may break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suctions on the legs are healthy and open, as they draw blood from all parts of the body, and relieve old pains of the thighs, uterus, bladder, and vulva, and draw out the hairs.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are on the thighs of the second feet, and the calves, and they all make the body weaker after long use, and cause pain in more positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	1. The manner of inserting the vacuum is to first empty it, and then place it firmly, and move it evenly, and continue doing this until you see the red and swollen part, and the appearance of pus.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	2. Then, clean them, and put the vacuums back in their place, as some have such severe pain and difficulty:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	3. If it is necessary to cut once only, and make wide wounds, and a proper size:
et suce legierement.	4. and gently suck:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	5. And if it is not big, and they cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtly cut the vein of great blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is not very fast, then it is likely to injure the third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we try to draw out little blood at a time, we only succeed once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we try to draw out much blood, we often return.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if it is not very fast, then it is better to stop and finish it if the patient's pulse is clearly felt, and those who have thick skin and are durable, and those who have rough edges, you should apply the ointment of opening and dissolving oils from the ointment of the oil openers.
