se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is made from olive oil, or honey-sweet almond oil, or sunflower seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is made from vegetable oil, such as mustard oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take olive oil, or balsam of Hermas, or olive oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is healthy and has large pores, it should not be oiled, but it should be washed after the application of vinegar of rose, or cold vinegar, or mushroom vinegar, or vinegar of porcelain, or other similar substances.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have moisture in their mouth, if they rise from silk, or vinegar of mustard, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive superfluities rise from wine vinegar, or ague of seuc, or decoction of anet or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not recommended to vinegar before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	For do not sleep after ventilation, and it is necessary that it wakes up when it should ventilate and when it is ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And if the healthy one is cold, and the unhealthy one is too hot and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it comes that he eats cold things, like lettuce and endive and spinach in milk, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and consume puddings, and hot cheese, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And if the one with a cold complexion eats honey syrup, and aromatic wine that is between winter and spring, and consumes little, and consumes puddings and thin soups and pies.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	When the joint is dislocated, if it needs to move more than a finger's width, it must be reset.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give certain people one time of triaicle or muscate before the dislocation, or afterward, to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	It is necessary to be subtle with the joint, but only those who are able to bear the pain should be dislocated.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The vents that are felt to be painful are those that are placed on the stomach, and on the thighs, and gout, and on the abdomen, and the bowels, and the rains, and the hainche, because this member does not suffer from pain in other parts, and only when it is attracting pain from one part to another, as we do with our breasts when they are sick.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	For the viscosity that is in the member, if we suck out the abdomen and the belly with cups to relieve the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And reduce the pain when it is inflamed or pierced, if by its virtue it attracts the inflammation, or if it leaves the pierce of the member.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And this is done when it is hung up in the belly and the mouth when it has inflammation retained, and these cups are administered empty by sucking only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And no time are they administered together with fire, and no time are they plained with cold tea, as in many diseases that cause the eyes to water, and in this way we fill the cup with hot water, or with water that has been boiled herbs, which are edible.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum device administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half palm-sized poles, and it has either cost as much as a thousand pennies, or less if the patient is small; so that it can be inserted like a needle, and it is made of steel, smooth in front so that it does not cut the helper's hand when putting it on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the environment, a wire of cross-grain steel or iron, to be held by a chisel, and it is large and small according to the diseases and the pain of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the bellies of children are not like knives, nor thin as fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And it must be placed on this ventouse on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	The cauterization candle or ointment should be applied, and it should be placed on the ventouse through the hole that is on the ventouse, so that the fire does not reach the inside of the ventouse and burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then it should be placed on the member, and you must see if the wound is as we have said, so that if you see vapor coming out, and then remove the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And apply the ointment as before, and repeat it often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse that is in the patient with the disease of pleurisy, at any age, there is no hole or wound, and it is not infected unless it is only when it is clear of fever and is placed on the member only.
et c’est li forme:	1. "And it is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without being stretched, they are not broken except in the limbs where it is not possible to put a ventouse due to their small size, like the lips and genitals, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in them of cartilage, if like two or three, and other similarities.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user if it is that when you find dislocations that are in soft waters and have a clear sensation of movement, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in soft water as they are related, and have no belly.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then clean the vein and the wound, then rub the limb as much as it is red, and put on the dislocations.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are flat, smooth, and well-placed, if it is the shoulder or arm that can be splinted, it is placed there, as this is best.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the shoulder, and then the elbow, well, and then straighten it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	If it is too late in the case of cold wrists, if the linen is too wet, then spread it out on a cool surface, and leave it until the wrists are not swollen.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	If the swelling increases, then put on vinegar or hot irons, and similar things, as long as it is not too much.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	If you cut half of the fevered limbs, and leave them as they are until they cool down on the limb, it will now be still.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more of them, take others that are fresher.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the wounds do not take the cloths, take the flesh of the limb freshly cut, or thrust a needle into it as much as it pains, and then insert them, and as they feel the warmth, they will cool down.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see them bleeding, if you powder some aloe and silk, or some charcoal, they will stop bleeding now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it treats of wounds and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	1. "If you are seeking knowledge about this chapter, it is not found in any ancient books, nor does any letter contain it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	2. "And for this reason, the science is lacking in our land, as I have never found any book.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	3. "And I do not know anything about it, because through the science of ancient books, I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by my habit in life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	4. "And I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the stumps that are amputated, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say this is the introduction of this book, the words and chapters, and the patient understands them, and learns the truth, if those who have experienced it can teach and learn this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting comes to any part of the body, if you hurry to heal the patient's shoulder from both sides, nothing will fail, as weak as it may be, whether from cold, children, or wounds.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	unless you tighten it not very tightly, or too loosely.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and do not use cold things, such as ice and hazelnut, and do not drink wine, nor use thin charcoal, and do not fill the veins with blood too much when you have no doubt of gangrene or expansion of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient reviews the treatment they used at their first government.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the meat that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, like wheat cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made of wool, and cheese, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling that is recovered, the fracture gets worse and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And you know that bones and joints broken cannot be well repaired or mended according to their nature due to the lack of members, nor those that are too soft, such as small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone and large tendons that are pulled and joined together as much as possible, just as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not to leave the work undone, and for this reason it is recommended to avoid large meals, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	The treatises of the physicians declare that there are many ways to break bones.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of fracturing in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that occurs when falling, and another when struck, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to have his engine and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes to his memory in his head.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known as the fracture of the bone because the bone is twisted, and it is well-apertured by itself, and some by pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when it does not have knots and is at the tip, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have knots, or a cut, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only move it with your hand, but put the medicine that comes after, and then pull it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you suspect that the fracture will be in the joint, and the two parts are dislocated, then you must now correctly align them, unless they cause death.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if they are spasmed and come, then leave it alone as long as the spasm is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then place it evenly in the muscle that you can lightly and wisely, and soothe that the restoration of it is lighter than the restorations of cells or if there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then pull it, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it is in the bone with broken pieces, if you stretch it by two parts, it is hands or fingers, or at your hand it is some small members, or at the cords, or at one cord and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, if by the parts of the broken member they are out of place, then reset them by using your fingers in the muscle that you can, and keep in mind that by your own hand does not come to the patient's pain or injury.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And carefully adjust the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	If it feels good in your hand, even if it seems not to be well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it grows well, and does not strain too much, do not press as they do who come by their incision and contraction to the member, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in its place, if the surgeon handles it well so that it does not move, neither by day nor by night, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the member is well secured so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not so, and it is necessary to put him in part of the body that does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him in place, so that twists do not come when he returns to it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I say.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I advise that the broken member is various in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For he has many limbs, which are divided and treated in the same way:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	if it is necessary to wrap them with linen cloths and fine threads.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like how a knee is treated.
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard linen, because the large bandages cover all the limbs, and they are tightened evenly, so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lie the entor is lightly bound with three or four turns, according to the member, and your hand is held tightly along the entire line, then go to the end of the fracture and it is tightened less than the fracture, which the fracture slightly moves away from the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the member a little and a little, as you grip a large part of the healthy shoulder, then take another line, and turn the entor upright on the broken member;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part opposite the fracture, and tighten it gently, do not pull too hard or too loosely, as we have said in the first line of this chapter;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place the threads between the stitches of linen or drapes, as they are equal, then tie them with silk and braid, and then put your well-made ends on, if there is no hemorrhage or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or hemorrhage, then put on something soothing for the hemorrhage and stopping the swelling, and leave it alone for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tighten your ends, and they should be of about one-third of a wide, sharp knife, or of wheat, or of dates, and they should be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the one who sets the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also be of the same length as it is required for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then tighten the bandage as you did in the first attempt, then tie a thread around it, as you did in the first attempt.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The more tightly it is wrapped, the less it is.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary that the thread be smooth, not too thick or too thin, and be of linen thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	Because if the thread is too thick, it is like the work of the fingers who make the laces of linen threads, and it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it only needs that there is less space between each stitch than the thickness of the lace.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the sharp edges of the stones after being washed with water, if they are not covered with linen or cloth, so that they do not freeze.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the tweezers, and the hair is broken, I will tell you the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not try to pull out all the broken bones at once, as it is dangerous.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not recommended to use these tools that are later than V years or VII, or according to the strength of your aposteme.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and then the manner of ancient splints to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and is that you take flour that is found in the mill's walls, mix it with a large amount of water, and make this concoction, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method for restoring fractures in other positions, as well as for women and children, because it is neither too wet nor too dry.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way to mend fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Prepare a mixture of oak bark, linen, and animal glue, mixed with Arabic gum, and add water in the ratio of 1:10.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mash and aloe, in the ratio of 1:2.
alechil VIIII З.;	Add alochil in the amount of 78%.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make a powder, and mix with egg whites.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the face is hot, then use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Other ways of measuring than by twist:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take a measure and a caliper, at least 10 centimeters;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	mark and incise, at least 7 centimeters;
acaice VI З.;	according to the size of the patient's hand;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	mix with arsenic X, and cook well, and add water or urine of the patient, and administer;
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Other ways of measuring joints and bones of the limbs, and alleviate pain, and the size is according to the bone, and fracture:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new cloth, and the oil in alcohol and cooked, and put on the limb;
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore flesh, but it is necessary to soothe the post-surgical pain and the true bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of splinting that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earth oak leaves, and mix them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make plasters for the repair of bone fractures and to help with the recovery of post-surgical pain.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, and a portion of flour from each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and mix with wine, and apply to the affected parts, and moisten with rose water or vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	2. Another way to apply it more frequently than the first, when the wound is firm, comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of valerian, linen seeds, mustard, honey, and a portion of each flower: violets and chamomile.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and mix with salt water or sweet vinegar, or with wine, according to the condition of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that it is not recommended to apply anything on the broken bone to restore its strength, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too wet nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen suggests that on the broken bone to restore, one should apply things like dry and warm substances such as mustard and aloe, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Other ways to mark injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take fingers and toes of the opposite hand, or hairs of the head, and nails, and cut them evenly, and the skin, and then make a mark.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then leave a small part afterwards, and take care not to hurt the patient's shoulder; if it does not move, do not move the bones of the shoulder.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not left by hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the shoulder, or itching, tenderness, or swelling, if you have time, and leave it, and then make the mark now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And gently unwrap it, and wet the mercury sponge, and dip it in cold water, and lift the leg up as much as the itch stops, and soothe the pain.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the leg rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moisten it with cold water or olive oil, and tie it tightly, as long as you are sure of not having a pulse.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And reduce the inflammation of the leg, and soothe the pain, then resume gently wrapping it, and a little bit of ointment, and do not strain it too much like before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And gently as it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the wound is gushed with blood and there is pain and swelling, and it is inflamed all over, and you have skill in plastering and bandaging, if it recurs, as you did at first properly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb that we have said, if it does not slip after three days or four or seven or ten.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never more than twenty days, according to what is seen, as long as the fracture sets, and approaches the bone to the splint.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	However, more restraint than before, and it will increase its flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb drying more than it should, advises that no herbs can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	When the fever rises, it often happens that you lose consciousness, and this happens every time, regardless of the type of day, and it lasts for a short while.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Due to this fever, the muscles in the limb are often injured, and they become weak, causing the member to be misaligned.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is harmful, and if it becomes more severe, I can only provide pain relief and advise proper treatment.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of wounds, and various shapes, and the causes are different.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are wounds that are caused by the impact of a spear, and the skin covers the entire bone, which is broken off from the bone, just like a hawk or a falcon.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For this reason, this method of fracture is called "hammering.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	The spear pierces the bone through various senses and is called this method of fracture "absolute.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And these are the wounds of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a thrust embedded, or cut, or from the bone after the piercing, or from the other side of the piercing, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which draws the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is under the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is healed in the bone as subtle as some chisels, and it is a small fissure, and for this it is called this fracture "capillary.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by cutting with a blade, or piercing with an awl, or seeming something else, and it lets the piece of bone enter, and it is the same as when they cut with hot iron when they forge the hammers;
si entre li piere dedens.	If it enters the piercing.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And furthermore, those who have been washed with wet water, like that of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and come in all these ways of fracture that are lightly broken if they were, so do these;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak to it in his shoulder;
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us consider all ways of fractures by the methods used for them, and by the corrupt char that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one has discovered the bone, and froths with their hand, if the dark fracture is open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep in mind as many accidents as possible of the midwife, and if you see no such accident, then like vomiting of cold, admission of understanding, extension, flexion, congestion, fever, and the wounds turning red and swelling, and other symptoms in various dispositions, if it cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the first pain comes to you, and it is in the shoulder, then it is necessary to stop the movement of the bone before the fourth month at the muse.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If this is the case, and you stop the movement of the bone before the ninth month, then the tendon of the bone will be corrupted, and the accident we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes near the girdle that encloses the collarbone, then you must cut off the damaged part;
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if you ignor the patient's pain and cut off the wet skin, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and reveal the wound more severe than you see, and if pus comes to cleanse the bone, or abscess ruptures, and you help it with what comes, and if you fill the shoulder with oiled flax;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	1. And make the wound rest as long as the inflammation is eased and it is assured of not dislocating.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	2. Then the bone begins to ossify, and it is made according to two methods of burning:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	3. One method is when you cut at the narrow end before, and it forms:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then, cut another piece of the same size as the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	4. And the second method is when you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	5. And in working lightly, so as not to blunt the blade:
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and thick, then it comes to pass that you percuss it with your hand, otherwise, if you maintain the edges with tapers, do not exceed the point of the bone, and it must have a margin or a circle that does not allow the point to pass over the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have more of them if many people come to their joints in the end of the bone, if you have tapers for your test.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality of percussing outside the broken bone is that you put the taper on the bone and turn it as much as necessary until you feel that the bone is perceived.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then, move the burn to another part a short while later, and then do everything thoroughly, then make the cuts into the bone that is between the holes, and do it more subtly than you please, and lightly, as we have said, as long as you take the bone out of your hand, or from any of the stirrups that you have, like nails, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and make sure you do not touch the brain or the sweat.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone perceived and cut, if it comes that you cover the wound that is made in the bone with the other instrument as an incisor, but it should be more narrow and more subtle than the other incision.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	If there is no movement of the small bones, neither heavy nor light scales, if the lighter bones slightly move.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then, treat the wounds and injuries that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of opening is when it is more difficult, which is the Galenic method.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the knife is very sharp, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the open fracture is visible, so that when you have removed this part, if you measure from the top of this incision, the form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And does not cut too much on one side, and the other part is turned towards the bone, if it is being cut.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then, with a small cut, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and be careful not to hit the cloth that is soaked.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is at the bone, if it is lightly on the bone, for it is felt quite painfully, and causes great fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only crushed by itself, and it has small pieces, if they cover the rough edges, and smooth the scales with a subtle rasping tool that you must have various quantities of, to adjust each joint according to the degree and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave in front of a coarse rasping tool, and then use a more subtle one, and continue doing this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair removal techniques and subtle wounds, it is necessary to follow their directions according to your needs.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	It is a matter that cannot be answered by anyone who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scar is discovered, then it is necessary to apply flax to the wound according to its size, and grease with rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another doubled gauze, and grease it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first gauze.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you can, so as not to burn the skin, then apply with other means and do not strain it too much, only as far as the wound allows.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it for one to two days, as long as the abscess is not suppurating, then remove it, and apply medicines such as roots of various plants, flour, powdered frankincense, aristolochic acid, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make powder from these things and apply it to the wound, and apply medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	The wound should be cleaned well, so you do not put on any ointment, nor do you assemble bows, because when bows are assembled on the skin, it often causes great pain to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	When something sharp is put on the wound, it may cause the patient great pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Preparation is necessary, as no accidents come to the patient if we follow what we have said, if it is doubtful, then there is doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if nothing is coming out of the wound except for medicine, then you must apply a part of honey, three parts of rose oil, and one part of glue, and then put the sharp thing on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, apply the wound in various ways that are safe and healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	1. If no party of the shoulder ever breaks, whether one or both, for they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	2. And the other is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is bowed or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	3. And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut the small dose or pertuss of the shoulder, and set the fracture at your index finger, and to the pouch as long as the bone does not return to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	4. And do this lightly, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the toe that is not the big toe, and it cannot be brought to the heel, then you should put it as even as possible at the end of a thick finger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of the second part, then if you repair it again, you will have to restore the first joint, if you please.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, then after the ninth or tenth day, when the wound is healed and the stitches are removed, and the fracture is in one place, then proceed with the treatment.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind one or another part, if the fracture has;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and the bandages be so large that they fill the abscesses with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	2. And no restorer would say that one must soothe the wounds with butter, and each one will die.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems to me that this is well, but it is necessary that they be made in the fashion of oven-baked wheat and milled mill powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent, as long as the bone is frozen, and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never once do they put their geese's wings in the tent, and if it is loosely draped and stays in place, and blows the air among.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or make what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms at the site while you are working, and it comes to the point where you put on a cloth or cotton cloth greased with rose oil, or in a small vial of laver.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the wound does not ooze, then apply plaster made of flour and powdered frankincense, mixed with beef broth, then place light spoons, and do not tie them too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the wound is small and broken into thin pieces, and they are broken into pieces that can be easily managed with this, then cut the fringes, and the treatment of things enchanted charms, and soothing, if like plasters and ointments can be easily managed with this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound or small wound, if it heals, and it puts on bandages, as soon as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not deep, but only slightly so, and it is not broken into pieces, but rather bent slightly, which can be corrected with a slight effort.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the left side, that you cut your index finger in the mouth of the midwife.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, then cut your index finger of the right hand, and lightly cut the fracture, and fix it with the other hand evenly, and hold.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	If the fracture of the lower jaw is described as Level II, and you intend to provide extension to the second part, as long as it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth move or fracture, if they are stretched from a gold or silver or silk thread, then put it on the broken jaw of the other side, and put two pieces of cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the wound a well-made cloth or a piece of leather long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it around the neck that you choose, and instruct the patient to lie down and give them light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	If you see that the figure changes, if it is lifted up, and then set it back to where it was.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply a paste made of flour from the bolter with a lot of urine or bread flour, after you have opened the wound.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And apply the paste on a light cloth, and when it is dry, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times, it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the wound is infected, then it comes to the attention of the physician, as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, the reward is a small piece of bone in the cast.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the osseous subtlety is easily covered by this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, it should be stretched according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all these pieces of bone, and there is none in vain, if the wound is wide, and it is large, and you put on flexible dressings, for mending it as much as possible, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks more times in front of, toward the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways.
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it is broken and separated in two, and has pieces, and it is the lighter to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operation is if the wound is as the fracture is with pain, that you have two assistants, if the one tint the helper that feels the forceful fracture.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and extend the other arm to the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the wound equal to your two sides, if it forms as it should, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have more to extend, then place the shoulder bone of the patient away from the wound a round sphere made of linen or wool, and it should be large according to your need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and gently apply the force, and pull the sphere to your hand so that you place the wound equally, if it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you do not take the head of the strong one away from its place, because it comes in front, then the patient will feel pain on their hateful side, and put their elbow or shoulder down, and bend the spine of the strong one as much as the bone of the strong one is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then attach the wound to your two sides, and if you have dislocated it, then it should be that you fix it back.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and take away the lighter pieces, and if the head cannot be joined by any means, if it is one of the ones you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you use the full force of this instrument to see if it will work:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, and is not too thin, and should be as wide as it is intended to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the will:
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and has two heads, if you see, and the larger ones are for larger wounds, and the smaller ones are for smaller wounds, according to the swelling of the wound you made when you treated the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	When you are sure of the incision, if there is pain, and if the wound is small, or if you doubt the incision, if you use the wound with dressings and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	2. And if aphrodisiacs are used, and it comes, if much oil is needed, and linseed and mustard, and wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The irritation of the bone is when it feels pain and tightness, it is that you apply to the bone the plaster of the ground and flour of oatmeal and a soft cloth, and a small amount of water, if you have the means.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very thick bandage from a palm leaf, then put the dough twice on the cloths, and apply it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin needle of three inches in length and one inch wide, and wrap the thread around it, so that the knot is at the end.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	Then place the needle on the bracelet, turn the thread around the loop, and remove the healthy nail, and remove the sick nail.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Then tighten each part, and when you see that the nail holds the bracelet firmly, and you see clearly that the thread does not hold the broken part, then reward each one, and when it is tightened, put on the restraint.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the sick nail on its back, and it puts a small hole on the other side of the shoe when it sleeps, to lift the helper to the top.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If you align the fracture of the bone by aligning the shoulder, or if you tie the arm to the collarbone, and it does not dislocate due to accidents, then it will be fine in about 20 years.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then continue the exercise, if you see that it is useful, and pull and release it as much as it needs to be restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it will be restored in 28 years, with no harm to anyone.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the injury to the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Only the shoulder breaks or becomes wide due to the bone, and it does not dislocate unless touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the acetabulum resembles the shape of the fracture, and it is adjusted according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then pour powdered mill with a lot of meal, and light spreads, and put on double fold.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a large and thin sheet, a bit larger than the shoulder, and if it is well fitted when the sheet is removed from the shoulder, if you use flax threads, then this sheet fits well.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then the strap is tightly tied with a large iron band, if the sheet does not move from its place, and watch the line each hour.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it is pulled apart, if it is held steady, and the head of the shoulder is forced out of its place, and the patient feels great pain on their chest;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the spine is restored in 20 days or 25;
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if it does not happen, and you are sure, because it is only the bones that are made to feel lighter;
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes before, and there is no sign of inflammation, then it is done, and the bone, and we do what we have said in the fracture of the force of reducing the swelling of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the bone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The weight is never broken in a million years, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the knee.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken outside, if it is dislocated, and it feels great pain, and there is lack of blood, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and the wounds are opened in the broken bones, and it feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is when the patient feels pain on their back, and the head of the shoulder is placed between the shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed, and the heads of the second ribs are assembled in your hands, and subtly put in place as much as the bone seems to fit;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then apply splints and bandages over the thin layer of salt, or another light substance, and wrap it around the broken bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and tighten the tie as much as possible around the back, and pull gently, and reward each hour with a drink, and if it relaxes, then tighten.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it hurts to uncover, either due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the limb, or pain or gangrene, if you haste, then uncover, and remove the splint, and attend to what has come from the ways of treatment.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the cauterization, and hold it firmly until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaching of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Fractures of the ribs only occur after great force is applied to the back, and at the top of the shoulder blades, and they do not displace unless they are greasy.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And it feels well in examination as it should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is if you place the breaching evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then place the plaster, and tighten with a needle, if you have the skill.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is inclined towards the shoulder blades, it feels very great pain and pressure, as if from tears, because the bone points to the cloth.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it aches all over, and often vomiting great quantities of blood, and this is very unhealthy, and the ancients have put much faith in it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it can be administered meat that inflames the belly, by pinching the nipple with the girdle.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, that challenging does not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, if it is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And say no one of those who put suction cups on the leg, to suck out the poison, and it seems right.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, it is not certain that the suction cup does not draw out the excess from the leg because of its weak position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And none of them would cover the shoulder with oily powdered lint, and then put tents between the ribs to measure the liver's turn, then treat the pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that points the girdle, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to break the costal cartilage of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put a suture instrument to hold the skin.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and therefore it is necessary to drill the bone, and draw lightly, and then cut the lips of the wound, if they are large, and cleanse them with emplausters as long as they are healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	If the abscess ruptures, if it comes with smooth oily cloths on the leg, and on the limb.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the limb while it is dislocating, and keep the cloths on the chest as needed, until it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never comes a fracture of the bone of the arm, and rarely does it happen that it breaks.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	When there is no pain, and you see whether it will be healthy or not, if you see your hands soft and swollen and lifeless, and cannot move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel any pain.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Dangerous are those that are mortally dislocated, and if they do not move and feel well when extracted and not stretched, dangerous are those who say the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if we put them in treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if something similar comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it is healthy or not, if you hold the bones in place, and if the accidents are those that are in the hands, and on the back there is a jump and a sense of wanting to vomit;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it is dislocated on its side, it suddenly ejects with will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When he is lying on his back and sees a shadow, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Sacrifices that are fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If he does not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come, if it is something lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if he complains of pain in his abscess, if you place on it ointment made from rose oil or oil of mustard plant, as long as it is soothing;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place on it a comforting plaster and wrap it in cloth, and tie it with a cord, and order the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as he is healthy;
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	If any bones break, then cover them with a cloth.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	If the bone is large, then sew the two sides of the wound together with strong stitches, and then apply ointment by anointing it with oil until it is healthy.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	If the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the bone," take your right hand pouch and put it in your left hand, then place the splint and clamp it on, if you are skilled at it.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then hold it tightly, and if it is broken further, then cut it off, and the bone, and treat the wound as much as it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	When the bone of the ankle is broken, and if it happens, unless there was already some pre-existing injury at the top;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and becomes long and twisted, and turns inward at the joints, and there comes pain to the leg, and swelling, and the broken part becomes inflamed;
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand as far as the broken bone;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and examine those that are the break and the shape of the bone;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the break is only at the top, then set it as straight as possible, so that it is in its natural position;
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it declines to the bone, then I order the patient to lie on his stomach as long as the restoration of this fracture is not clear.
